      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alison Morgan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alison Morgan" href="/user/show/1579566-alison-morgan">Alison Morgan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69855392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7994551311334723653">I LOVE Anne Tyler. Every time I sit down to write a novel (haha, that sounds really funny) I draw on Anne Tyler and Jane Austen for inspiration, because I love the way they make an ordinary person/family, and the minutiae of their daily lives, so fascinating. Argh! If only I could do that, I wouldn't have to spend tons of money and time on a law school education - I could just sit back and let the royalties roll in. Anyway, Anne Tyler as a writer is totally realistic, eccentric, funny, sad, and </span>
  <span id="freeText7994551311334723653" style="display:none">I LOVE Anne Tyler. Every time I sit down to write a novel (haha, that sounds really funny) I draw on Anne Tyler and Jane Austen for inspiration, because I love the way they make an ordinary person/family, and the minutiae of their daily lives, so fascinating. Argh! If only I could do that, I wouldn't have to spend tons of money and time on a law school education - I could just sit back and let the royalties roll in. Anyway, Anne Tyler as a writer is totally realistic, eccentric, funny, sad, and unexpected, and she is never more so than in Saint Maybe. I love Ian, the main character, a normal kid who carries a burden of guilt that turns him into a tragic, not so normal, but really wonderful man. I love the kids he adopts - poor humourless Agatha, sad little Thomas, and sweet, mischevious Daphne. This book is epic, really, following the family through years and years of their lives. In fact, when I think of this book, it makes my throat burn with unshed tears - haha, melodramatic, but totally true. Not everyone loves Anne Tyler, but those people . . . I just can't understand. She is brilliant, and in my opinion, this book is her best. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7994551311334723653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364471799?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/1135162-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1135162-debra?shelf=mainstream-literary-fiction">mainstream-literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364471799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11850361114346371215">Life is going well for eighteen-year-old Ian Bedloe. He has great parents, a girlfriend, a newlywed brother, Danny, and college in his future. But Danny’s fatal car crash darkens Ian’s world. He feels anger, guilt, and partial responsibility for what might well be his brother’s suicide.<br/> <br/>Saint Maybe is a compelling story about different types of loss, and the ramifications of life-changing moments. The book made me want to keep reading to see what happens to Ian. I wanted him and other characters</span>
  <span id="freeText11850361114346371215" style="display:none">Life is going well for eighteen-year-old Ian Bedloe. He has great parents, a girlfriend, a newlywed brother, Danny, and college in his future. But Danny’s fatal car crash darkens Ian’s world. He feels anger, guilt, and partial responsibility for what might well be his brother’s suicide.<br /> <br />Saint Maybe is a compelling story about different types of loss, and the ramifications of life-changing moments. The book made me want to keep reading to see what happens to Ian. I wanted him and other characters to make better choices, but knew they couldn’t, or wouldn’t, yet the ending was satisfying.<br /><br />The first few chapters changed point of view, so I’d assumed the central characters would each be given attention, however POV becomes almost exclusively Ian’s after eighty pages. The tale is simply yet beautifully told, and while often sad, it was also filled with a lot of heart and hope. Anne Tyler is a Pulitzer Prize winner for her novel Breathing Lessons. If you hadn’t known this, you wouldn’t be surprised after reading this book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11850361114346371215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_50820097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50820097" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2165864-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442514058p2/2165864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50820097?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/2165864-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50820097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12037222523591295378">One of my favorite books of all time. Tyler has an unrivaled talent for describing the small details, the quiet moments, and somehow weaves an entire character's life from these seemingly small details and quiet moments. She has mastered the brushstroke technique, and this is particularly apparent in Saint Maybe. This tale of redemption focuses on Ian Bedloe, a young man who, in a moment of impatient irritation, a moment that could happen to any of us, unthinkingly causes a terrible tragedy in h</span>
  <span id="freeText12037222523591295378" style="display:none">One of my favorite books of all time. Tyler has an unrivaled talent for describing the small details, the quiet moments, and somehow weaves an entire character's life from these seemingly small details and quiet moments. She has mastered the brushstroke technique, and this is particularly apparent in Saint Maybe. This tale of redemption focuses on Ian Bedloe, a young man who, in a moment of impatient irritation, a moment that could happen to any of us, unthinkingly causes a terrible tragedy in his family. Saint Maybe chronicles the rippling aftereffects of this tragedy, and Ian's attempts to redeem himself. I've read this book so many times that I've gone through two paperback copies and should probably invest in a hardback. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12037222523591295378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This was different than others in that it was not about adult relationships as much as about a single character and his relationship with his parents and the children he helps to raise.   <span id="freeText8172344368059980907" style="display:none">I keep thinking about this book. An unexpected tragedy puts the main character in a position to take on an unwanted burden. He accepts he responsibility and does it ever so well, changing his life and those around him for the better.<br /><br />I love Anne Tyler's books. This was different than others in that it was not about adult relationships as much as about a single character and his relationship with his parents and the children he helps to raise. The book moves along slowly, which I liked, because it allows the characters to emerge and change over the years in a way that seems real and natural. I also really liked the portrayal of the religious piece. In some ways quirky, but Ian's commitment and the person it helps him to become is very substantial and inspiring. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365638207" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16857007908558285214">Engrossing, moving, and thoroughly sentimental. <br/><br/>This novel is not perfect in the least, but it is unquestionably something to think about. Even middle class, white, wholesome families inhabiting the all-American suburbia have depth to them (is primarily what I gained from this story). Well-fleshed people, not characters, are what comprise this story--something not many other novels that I have read can boast.<br/><br/>Side-note: the Middle Eastern foreigners are a static (but absolutely hilarious!) additi</span>
  <span id="freeText16857007908558285214" style="display:none">Engrossing, moving, and thoroughly sentimental. <br /><br />This novel is not perfect in the least, but it is unquestionably something to think about. Even middle class, white, wholesome families inhabiting the all-American suburbia have depth to them (is primarily what I gained from this story). Well-fleshed people, not characters, are what comprise this story--something not many other novels that I have read can boast.<br /><br />Side-note: the Middle Eastern foreigners are a static (but absolutely hilarious!) addition. They are all composed of one mindset, but nonetheless, add an invigorating spice to the story. This novel, in other words, is as quietly humorous as it is tragic. Contradictory, but also quite fitting.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ryTr34+wXBHhZ6taYsN5PqKqDhrqN9kCpUlidprsHRrlh7f5CpTX92MRuwjvnTWDg+tVgFW6Hj45OceuOY/ybw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A2A6rFApX35mxqhLOjf5GV17O+alG7D3s6MuqXQ0xgJJw2aK1Q3UmOSwuBm3abWkfDpgfBqWd8sv04tx11cpdw==')})
  }

His investigations into Jackson\'s failing health made headlines around the globe. Six months later, the King of Pop was dead.Whatever the final autopsy results reveal, it was greed that killed Michael Jackson. Friends and associates paint a tragic picture of the last years and days of his life as Jackson made desperate attempts to prepare for the planned concert series at London\'s 02 Arena in July 2009. <span id="freeTextContainer13611806268008094387">Anne Tyler was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. She has published 20 novels, her debut novel being <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112321.If_Morning_Ever_Comes' title='If Morning Ever Comes' rel='nofollow noopener'>If Morning Ever Comes</a>
</i> in (1964). Her eleventh novel, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons' title='Breathing Lessons' rel='nofollow noopener'>Breathing Lessons</a>
</i>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a mem</span>
  <span id="freeText13611806268008094387" style="display:none">Anne Tyler was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. She has published 20 novels, her debut novel being <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112321.If_Morning_Ever_Comes" title="If Morning Ever Comes" rel="nofollow noopener">If Morning Ever Comes</a>
</i> in (1964). Her eleventh novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons" title="Breathing Lessons" rel="nofollow noopener">Breathing Lessons</a>
</i>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters.</span>
